## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration A in a chemical reaction system. The rate law dA/dt is typically a function of concentration A (and possibly time t for non-autonomous systems), following well-established kinetic rate law forms from zero-order through complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order / reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with constant source/equilibrium)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate law from reversible reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed saturation kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis with finite capacity)
- Cubic autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)**2 (higher-order autocatalytic mechanism)
- Time-modulated first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Competing pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (parallel reactions with different orders)
- Sigmoidal cooperativity (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Linear with time source: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (first-order decay with time-dependent input)
- Fractional-order decay with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant production)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration-only dependence (no explicit t) suggests a true autonomous rate law from a reaction mechanism
- Explicit time dependence in dA/dt suggests externally driven conditions (temperature program, light intensity variation) or elimination of coupled species
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate enzyme or catalytic mechanisms with saturation
- Product terms A*(c-A) indicate autocatalytic or logistic behavior where A catalyzes its own formation up to a limit
- Negative integer or half-integer power-law exponents on A suggest chain reaction or radical mechanisms
- Polynomial rate laws in A (quadratic, cubic) often arise from elementary reaction steps combined via mass action
- If dA/dt changes sign at specific A values, equilibrium or steady-state concentrations exist, suggesting terms like c0*(A - c1) or c0*A*(A - c1)
- Fractional exponents on concentration (e.g., A**0.5) indicate radical chain mechanisms or diffusion-limited kinetics
